## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, indicating a continuous-time population dynamics model. With features (t, P), common structures include per-capita growth laws (functions of P), density dependence, Allee effects, harvesting/immigration, and explicit time-varying (seasonal or trending) rates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth rate)
- Linear birth–death with net rate: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (immigration/emigration offset plus proportional growth/decline)
- Density-dependent quadratic loss: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding/competition as pairwise interactions when c1 < 0)
- Cubic self-limitation: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects / multiple interaction scales)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (equivalently c0 * P * log(K / P) after reparameterization; slowing growth with log-density dependence)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence; c2 = 1 reduces to standard logistic)
- Richards / generalized logistic (shape parameter): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (adds asymmetry/shape control beyond theta-logistic)
- Allee effect (strong Allee, cubic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low density; multiple equilibria including extinction threshold)
- Allee effect (weak Allee via per-capita term): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P**2 (positive density dependence at low P through +P^2 term)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 (c2 < 0 models fixed quota removal independent of P)
- Proportional harvesting / mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (net rate reduced by per-capita removal)
- Seasonal forcing (time-varying rate): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * cos(c2 * t)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Time-trending growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slowly changing environment or management over time)
- Self-limitation with saturating carrying effect: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 / (1 + c2 * P) (competition that saturates at high density)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth analysis: If (dP_dt / P) is approximately constant, expect dP_dt ∝ P (exponential growth/decay); if (dP_dt / P) decreases with P, expect negative density dependence terms (e.g., -P^2, -(P^theta)).
- Equilibria counting via factorization: Multiple biologically meaningful equilibria often appear as products like P*(a*P-1)*(1-b*P), indicating extinction (P=0), Allee threshold, and carrying-capacity-type equilibria.
- Allee signature at low density: dP_dt < 0 for small positive P but > 0 for intermediate P suggests a factor (c*P-1) or additional +P^2 term creating positive density dependence at low P.
- Seasonality cue: Regular oscillations in residuals versus t suggest adding sin(c*t) and cos(c*t) modulation on P (time-varying per-capita rates).
- Harvesting/immigration cue: Nonzero dP_dt when P ≈ 0 suggests an additive constant term (immigration if positive, constant-yield harvest if negative).
- Crowding mechanism cue: If dP_dt falls roughly linearly with P at high densities, a -P^2 term is typical; if decline is sharper/shallower than quadratic, consider -(P^theta) or adding cubic terms.
- Asymmetry in approach to equilibrium: If growth slows very early or late relative to a symmetric logistic curve, consider Gompertz (log term) or Richards-type exponents to shift inflection behavior.
- Time-trend cue: Systematic drift in inferred growth rate over time (even at similar P) suggests r(t) structures like (c0 + c1*t) or exp(c0 + c1*t) multiplying P.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG15)
============================================================
GT: c0*P**c1 + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)
Candidate formulas: 53

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,P)=0.4866911314650416\,P^{1/3}+0.4866911314650416\,P\,e^{-0.08577402101126279\,t}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly** “(constant)\(P^{1/3}\) + (constant)\(P\exp(\text{linear in }t)\)” and **nothing else** (any extra term must be made identically 0 for all \(t,P\)).

---

### 1. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3\log(c4 t+1)\sin(Pc5+c6)\)
Set \(c3=0\). Then choose \(c0=0.4866911314650416,\; c1=0.4866911314650416,\; c2=-0.08577402101126279\). Matches GT.

### 2. \(P^{c0}c1e^{c2 t} + c3 + c4e^{c5 t}\sin(Pc6+c7)\)
To match GT we need a \(P^{1/3}\) term **without** \(t\)-dependence and a \(P e^{kt}\) term. This form ties \(P^{c0}\) to an exponential in \(t\), so you can’t get a pure \(P^{1/3}\) term unless \(c2=0\), but then you lose the needed \(e^{-0.0857 t}\) factor. No way to get both required terms simultaneously. Not a match.

### 3. \(Pc0 + Pc1(Pc2)^{c3} + P^{c4}c5e^{c6 t} + c7 t\)
Has no standalone \(P^{1/3}\) term unless you force \(c4=1/3\) and \(c6=0\), giving \(c5P^{1/3}\). But then you still need \(P e^{-0.0857 t}\); the only exponential term is tied to \(P^{c4}\), not \(P\), unless \(c4=1\), which conflicts. Also must kill \(c7 t\) and other \(P\)-power terms. Can’t produce both GT terms. Not a match.

### 4. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2 + P^{c3}c4e^{c5 t} + c6 t (P+c7)^{1/5}\)
Need \(P^{1/3}\) term: could set \(1+c0=1/3\Rightarrow c0=-2/3\) and use \(c1\) to scale, but then that term is \(P^{1/3}\) yes. Need \(P e^{kt}\): would require \(c3=1\). Then you have extra \(Pc2\) unless \(c2=0\), and must kill last term by \(c6=0\). This leaves \(c1P^{1/3}+c4P e^{c5 t}\), which can match GT by choosing \(c1=0.486691...\), \(c4=0.486691...\), \(c5=-0.085774...\). So it **can** match.

### 5. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3 + Pc4e^{c5 t} + Pc6\)
Set \(c1=c2=c3=c6=0\). Then choose \(c0=0.486691...\), \(c4=0.486691...\), \(c5=-0.085774...\). Matches.

### 6. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3\log(c4e^{Pc5+c6 t}+1)\)
Extra log term depends on \(P,t\); only way to remove it for all \(P,t\) is \(c3=0\). Then same as GT by setting \(c0,c1,c2\) appropriately. Matches.

### 7. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3 t/(Pc4+c5) + c6/(Pc4+c5)\)
Must eliminate rational terms: set \(c3=c6=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 8. \(Pc0 + Pc1(Pc2)^{c3} + Pc4e^{c5 t} + c6 t (P+c7)^{1/5}\)
No \(P^{1/3}\) term available (all main terms are proportional to \(P\) times something). Even if \(c1(Pc2)^{c3}\) gives \(P^{1/3}\) inside, it’s multiplied by \(P\) giving \(P^{1+c3}\). Not a match.

### 9. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2 + P^{c3}c4e^{c5 t} + c6\log(Pc7+1) + c8 t (P+c9)^{1/5}\)
Can match like candidate 4 by setting \(c0=-2/3\), \(c3=1\), \(c2=0\), and kill extras with \(c6=0\), \(c8=0\). Then choose \(c1,c4,c5\) to match constants/exponent. Matches.

### 10. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3/(c4e^{c5 t}+1)\)
The last term depends on \(t\) only; GT has no such additive term. Only removable by \(c3=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 11. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + Pc3/(c4 t+c5) + c6/(c4 t+c5)\)
Extra terms are rational in \(t\); must set \(c3=c6=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 12. \(P^{c0}c1e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4e^{c5 t} + c6\)
Need one term to be \(P^{1/3}\) with no \(t\)-dependence: set \(c0=1/3,\; c2=0,\; c1=0.486691...\).
Need other term \(P e^{-0.0857 t}\): set \(c3=1,\; c5=-0.085774...,\; c4=0.486691...\).
Set \(c6=0\). Matches.

### 13. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3e^{c4 t}\log(Pc5+1)\)
Log term depends on \(P\); only removable by \(c3=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 14. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3 t/(c4 t+c5) + c6/(c4 t+c5)\)
Extra \(t\)-rational terms must be removed: set \(c3=c6=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 15. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2e^{c3 t} + Pc4\)
Kill \(P^2\) and extra linear \(P\): set \(c1=0,\; c4=0\). Then choose \(c0=0.486691...\), \(c2=0.486691...\), \(c3=-0.085774...\). Matches.

### 16. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + Pc3(1-(Pc4)^{c5})^{c6}\)

### 17. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + Pc3/(Pc4+c5) + c6/(Pc4+c5)\)
Extra rational-in-\(P\) terms must be removed: set \(c3=c6=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 18. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + Pc3(c4+t)^{c5}\)
Extra factor \((c4+t)^{c5}\) must be identically 0 or 1. Easiest: set \(c3=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 19. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + Pc3 + Pc4 t\)

### 20. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3\log(c4 t+1)\)

### 21. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4e^{c5 t}\)
To equal GT (which has exactly two terms), the third term must be identically 0: set \(c4=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 22. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + Pc3\log(c4/(P+c5)+1)\)

### 23. \(P^{c0}c1 + P^{c2}c3e^{c4 t}\)
Set \(c0=1/3,\; c1=0.486691...\). Set \(c2=1,\; c3=0.486691...\), \(c4=-0.085774...\). Matches.

### 24. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3\log(Pc4+1)\)
Extra \(\log(Pc4+1)\) must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 25. \(Pc0e^{c1 t} + c2 + c3\log(c4e^{P^{1/3}c5}+1)\)
No separate \(P^{1/3}\) additive term; log term is not a pure power and depends on \(P^{1/3}\) inside an exponential/log. Also constant offset \(c2\) must be 0. Even with \(c3=0\), you only have \(P e^{c1 t}\), missing \(P^{1/3}\). Not a match.

### 26. \(P^{c0}c1e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4 + c5\)
To get \(P^{1/3}\) term without \(t\): could set \(c0=1/3,c2=0\). To get \(P e^{-0.0857 t}\) you’d need an exponential on the \(P^1\) term, but second term has no \(t\). Not possible. Not a match.

### 27. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + c3 t^{c4}\)
Extra \(t^{c4}\) term must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 28. \(Pc0/(P+c1) + P^{c2}c3 + P^{c4}c5e^{c6 t}\)
Need exactly \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P e^{kt}\). You can set \(c2=1/3,c3=0.486691...\). Set \(c4=1,c5=0.486691...,c6=-0.085774...\). But must remove \(Pc0/(P+c1)\). That term cannot be identically 0 unless \(c0=0\). Do that. Then it matches. Matches.

### 29. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4/(P^{c3}+c5)\)
Extra fraction term must be 0: set \(c4=0\). Then match with \(c0,c1,c2\). Matches.

### 30. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + Pc3 + c4\)

### 31. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1/(Pc2+1) + Pc3e^{c4 t}\)

### 32. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4\)
